  <i>...THE FIREMAN IS COMING.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467398680ra/19588748.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I gave the book 4 stars because there is a part that lagged for me, but it's still awesome! <br><br>I'm assuming everyone knows there is a disease going around and if you catch the spore your skin becomes dragonscale. And then later on you burst into flame! Yay! NOT! <br><br>One of the main characters in the book is Harper and she is a very nice nurse. She sings to kids and people at the hospital and she's just a very nice person. She has an arse of a husband named Jakob and I loathed him. I was hoping someone would just set him on fire! <br><br>The Fireman himself doesn't make too many appearances in the book, but when he does he's always helping someone and bringing them back to the camp. Which turned into some kind of psycho cult place after the leader was sick. The Fireman stayed away from the camp until he was needed and there are reasons that he didn't come help when things went bad. I won't tell you, spoilers and all. <br><br>The people at the came have found a way to control burning in a blaze of glory. It's called the Bright and you need to read the book to learn more about that as well. I think it is totally cool. BUT, there is something else they can do, well some of them can do that is really cool. There are certain benefits of having the disease and I would like to be on the winning side! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467500130i/19599821._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are a lot of characters in the book that I really loved and some I didn't of course. At one point though someone is stealing special things from each person. I was really mad when I found out the story behind that issue. <br><br>Overall, the book is really good and I'm glad it's part of my collection :-) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467500130i/19599822._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Enjoy! ♥<br><br>PS ~ Read all of the stuff at the back of the book because there is some extra book included :-)<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/07/the-fireman-by-joe-hill.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_1523477535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1523477535" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33359750-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576550045p2/33359750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1523477535?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/33359750-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26222107-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1523477535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5785847084814132594">I'll admit that I had high expectations for this book, and while I didn't love it, I still enjoyed it tremendously. I went back and forth on rating it at 3 or 4 stars, but 4 eventually seemed right. The Dragonscale virus is a doozy. There were a few instances when the story dragged, but I can't say that I was ever bored by it. I think what I really wanted more of was character development. I liked Harper, and the way she went from meek and mild, to a strong woman, but I wanted more. I loved the </span>
  <span id="freeText5785847084814132594" style="display:none">I'll admit that I had high expectations for this book, and while I didn't love it, I still enjoyed it tremendously. I went back and forth on rating it at 3 or 4 stars, but 4 eventually seemed right. The Dragonscale virus is a doozy. There were a few instances when the story dragged, but I can't say that I was ever bored by it. I think what I really wanted more of was character development. I liked Harper, and the way she went from meek and mild, to a strong woman, but I wanted more. I loved the fireman, but his personality could have been even more enhanced, and I hated how he was always getting broken! Broken bones everywhere! Also, I think Joe was paying a bit of homage to his Dad, and his story The Stand. Nick, a deaf mute, a pregnant Harper Francis, "May I call you Frannie?" Also, the reference to Nozz-a-la cola. I kept expecting Randall Flagg to come screaming around the corner driving his Takura Spirit! These little things kept taking me out of the story. Still, as a whole I'm pretty satisfied with the book, and it may even be one I'd read again. Yep, I'd recommend this book and author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5785847084814132594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1650316666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1650316666" />
    <a title="Evans Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7008067-evans-light"><img alt="Evans Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567305260p2/7008067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1650316666?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evans Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evans Light" href="/user/show/7008067-evans-light">Evans Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062200631" href="/book/show/25816688-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650316666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18142266418297239659"><b>
  <i>If you dislike unpopular opinions, then please don't read this review. I'm breaking from the pack on this one.<br/><br/>I didn't want to, trust me. But here we are:</i>
</b><br/><br/>This is the book I've been eagerly awaiting since I finished his five-star NOS4A2, only it wasn't.<br/><br/>Joe Hill's <b>THE FIREMAN.</b><br/><br/>Rambling, corn-pone, cartoonish.<br/>Unlikable characters, interminable dialogue, zero forward momentum.<br/><br/>Other than a mild dislike of the second half of HORNS (which was basically a retelling of the first half), I'm a huge fan </span>
  <span id="freeText18142266418297239659" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>If you dislike unpopular opinions, then please don't read this review. I'm breaking from the pack on this one.<br /><br />I didn't want to, trust me. But here we are:</i>
</b><br /><br />This is the book I've been eagerly awaiting since I finished his five-star NOS4A2, only it wasn't.<br /><br />Joe Hill's <b>THE FIREMAN.</b><br /><br />Rambling, corn-pone, cartoonish.<br />Unlikable characters, interminable dialogue, zero forward momentum.<br /><br />Other than a mild dislike of the second half of HORNS (which was basically a retelling of the first half), I'm a huge fan of Joe Hill's work prior to this book. 20th CENTURY GHOSTS is one of my all-time favorite collections, and NOS4A2 is a Top-10 novel for me.<br /><br />But THE FIREMAN has left this reader's love affair singed, if not in total ashes.<br /><br />Bear in mind, this review is coming from someone who hasn't been able to find his way to the end of a Stephen King novel since TOMMYKNOCKERS (UNDER THE DOME being the sole exception, and that just barely), so I'm likely an outlier in opinion on this one. I like my fiction lean and mean, and this book was neither. If you're a fan of Stephen King's output from the last couple of decades, then by all means ignore this review and go enjoy THE FIREMAN. This book is for you. It very much emulates the modern King's unhurried storytelling style (although the down-home voice is somewhat less successfully replicated).<br /><br />It's a shame though, at least to this reader, because the premise of this book was certainly intriguing enough and "Book One" (the first 113 pages) delivered on that promise with sleek, gripping prose.<br /><br />Then it appears as though the editor fell asleep on the job or quit altogether, because the story literally ground to a halt, caught in a morass of endless inane character backstories conveyed in some of the corniest cheeseball dialogue I've seen this century. There is some damn fine prose laced throughout this slog of a story, to be sure; like his dad, Joe Hill can write like nobody's business, but Joe Hill deserves an editor with an iron fist and bloody scalpel-shaped red pen.<br /><br />The unrelenting parade of forced references littered throughout struck me as cloying, not clever, and only served to remind me of the fact that the entertainment value of little Easter egg games diminishes rapidly while literally hundreds of pages are grinding by with nothing more happening than people acting cute while the world burns. Bored to the breaking point, I stoically pushed through to the end after concluding "Book Five" (page 388) hoping to find something of interest, yet my frantic search left me empty-handed.<br /><br />Some serious editing could have turned this book into an exceptional 350 page novel, rather than the 750 page mess it ended up being. Here's to hoping Joe Hill doesn't follow closely in his father's footstep of releasing increasingly muddled doorstop novels, but I'm guessing that ship has already sailed. He's got bigger ambitions than being a horror writer, I suppose, and the success of this book is likely to propel him much further in that direction.<br /><br />Godspeed, Joe. Hope to see you around these parts again someday.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18142266418297239659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062200631" href="/book/show/25816688-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer14607981568505122592">This was an honestly fascinating ride of a novel. I wasn't entirely certain what to expect because of some reviews, but I'm certainly happy I got to read it. I was also a bit more satisfied with the ending than I thought I would be.<br/><br/>So what's the big deal with Hill's big novel? <br/><br/>Is it really an origin story for a handful of firestarters among a whole world's spontaneous combustion? A survival tale against the hate and fear riddled remnants of "clean" humanity? One of those ever-decreasing remnants</span>
  <span id="freeText14607981568505122592" style="display:none">This was an honestly fascinating ride of a novel. I wasn't entirely certain what to expect because of some reviews, but I'm certainly happy I got to read it. I was also a bit more satisfied with the ending than I thought I would be.<br /><br />So what's the big deal with Hill's big novel? <br /><br />Is it really an origin story for a handful of firestarters among a whole world's spontaneous combustion? A survival tale against the hate and fear riddled remnants of "clean" humanity? One of those ever-decreasing remnants of post-apocalyptic SF that's actually designed for adults?<br /><br />Yeah, it's all of those, and more. I really enjoyed having an 26 year old MC nurse who's pregnant and learning how to live with or become a human flamethrower.<br /><br />It's just not that common.<br /><br />Comic books aside, of course, but this novel is not a comic book origin story at all. It's a survival fiction and it's also a pretty tight commentary on sheeple and social media and popular pundits. It's also pretty heartwarming and horrifying and an oddly powerful and persuasive argument for finding peace in our hearts. :)<br /><br />I liked that bit the most. It kinda rocked.<br /><br />Everything is going to hell, but the only way through it is by peace. Um... With benefits. :)<br /><br />I had a really good time with this one. Thank goodness I gave it a shot. :) Maybe it's better because I lowered my expectations, but whatever, it's good. :) Loved the pyrotechnics. :)</span>

<div id="review_1841786999" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1841786999" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1841786999?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062200631" href="/book/show/25816688-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1841786999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12313236949668316074">Joe Hill made quite the 'spark' with this novel, which garnered a significant following in 2016, culminating in winning one of the Goodreads awards for its genre. With curiosity piqued and a gap in my reading requirements, I chose to dive in while trying to steer clear of the ripples and spoilers that others have left around me. Harper Grayson is a school nurse with little of interest going on in her life, though the world is coming apart at the proverbial seams. People from every corner of the </span>
  <span id="freeText12313236949668316074" style="display:none">Joe Hill made quite the 'spark' with this novel, which garnered a significant following in 2016, culminating in winning one of the Goodreads awards for its genre. With curiosity piqued and a gap in my reading requirements, I chose to dive in while trying to steer clear of the ripples and spoilers that others have left around me. Harper Grayson is a school nurse with little of interest going on in her life, though the world is coming apart at the proverbial seams. People from every corner of the earth are developing what the medical profession has labelled draco incendia trychophyton, known in the vernacular as 'dragonscale'. It appears on the skin as a grey scaly rash and can progressively envelop more of the carrier's body, changing colour at times as well. Dragonscale is highly contagious, though no one seems sure how it passes from one human to another. What everyone has come to see is that carriers can show signs of billowing smoke from their hands and feet, like a small collection of dry kindling. As the carrier's illness develops, spontaneous combustion is also possible, though the general public has been given little knowledge of the events and this leaves them to turn against the infected. Carriers are pariahs and try to hide their plight, fearful of 'cremation crews', tasked to seeking to kill those who carry the condition before it can spread further. One such crew is headed by the Marlboro Man, who encapsulates the rugged cowboy and keeper of the peace while slaying the sick as quickly as he can locate them. Harper soon realises that she has been infected, which places an irreparable wedge between her and husband, Jakob. Even after he finds out Harper is expecting their first child, Jakob tries to banish her and does all he can to push added levels of isolation. Harper rages back and soon encounters a fireman-cum-pyromancer, John Rookwood, who has a small following of infected individuals. They lead her to an abandoned and secluded camp where other carriers are living. This camp, a collective of sorts, struggles with the daily worries around being hunted by 'cremation crews' and the inner struggle of any group seeking self-sustenance. Fractures within the group develop and soon Harper witnesses a mutiny, all while she tries to learn more about draco incendia trychophyton. Rookwood remains distanced from the group, though he and Harper share a strong connection and his insights are supported by a previous collective member who was murdered for his attempts to push back against the societal ostracism. While she learns how to tame the progress of dragonscale in a melodious manner, Harper has major hurdles ahead if she wants to survive, while the world is bent on killing those who differ too greatly. Hill does a fascinating job of developing this story on many levels and lures the reader in, be they interested in the story, the metaphors, or the microcosm found within the narrative. Well worth the hype it has received and should be high on the list of readers who need a little horror and entertainment any time of year.<br /><br />Hill has writing pulsing through his veins, with both parents highly acclaimed authors in their own rights. He does not try to grab hold of their coattails to be effective, carving out a niche all his own and remains highly successful in this venture. His writing does have some parallels to that of his father, perhaps in the oddities in which he places his characters, but there is a definite uniqueness in the flow and the tangents presented to the captivated reader. The invested reader will see this novel as being something other than a collection of sick individuals who are in hiding, finding parallels with the proverbial leper colony in which people are thrown when the general public is not aware or given sufficient information on which to base an educated decision. The struggles are not unique or off the wall, though Hill effectively creates a character base to lure the reader into significant sympathy. Additionally, Hill touches on the in-fighting of any isolated community as group and personal politics cloud the larger struggle, that of survival. Hill's ever-advancing narrative and swath of different characters provides the greatest Petri dish for effective political meltdown. Again, one might see this as a great microcosm of the larger human struggle for success, where those who are too alike tend to clash and forget the thread that ties them all together. I know I used to bemoan English teachers who asked students to look below the story to find these themes, but they seem so apparent and Hill develops these struggles so effortlessly that the reader cannot help but peer through the smoke and blazing to notice them. Hill does not shy away from generalities, perhaps painting the English as a potty-mouth group who curse so uniquely that North Americans could tear out a page from their verbal playbook. However, it has moments of humour, alongside a protagonist whose unusual obsession with Julie Andrews and her depiction of Mary Poppins keeps readers constantly shaking their heads. If this novel is anything like the other work that Hill has produced, I will be sure to rush forward to dive headlong into those, though my reading list is growing daily.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Hill for a wonderful way to start my 2017 reading journey. You offered a light at the end of the tunnel, though tossed in enough smoke and mirrors to keep me guessing.<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a></span>

<div id="review_1441711698" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441711698" />
    <a title="Char " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6581119-char"><img alt="Char " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415394568p2/6581119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1441711698?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Char " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Char " href="/user/show/6581119-char">Char </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26222107-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=dark-fiction">dark-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=wickedly-disturbing">wickedly-disturbing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=horror-after-dark-reviews">horror-after-dark-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1441711698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6428381898739353430"> 4.5 stars!<br/><br/>Dragonscale! It's a disease, a plague really, that etches one's skin with what looks like black hieroglyphics. Unfortunately, at some point the hieroglyphs light up and burst into flame and when they do, it's all over for you. If you happen to be standing next to anything flammable, it all over for that, (or them), too. <br/> <br/>The world as we know it falls apart due to the 'scale, and people react much as you think they would. Picture how Donald Trump would react to people bursting into fla</span>
  <span id="freeText6428381898739353430" style="display:none"> 4.5 stars!<br /><br />Dragonscale! It's a disease, a plague really, that etches one's skin with what looks like black hieroglyphics. Unfortunately, at some point the hieroglyphs light up and burst into flame and when they do, it's all over for you. If you happen to be standing next to anything flammable, it all over for that, (or them), too. <br /> <br />The world as we know it falls apart due to the 'scale, and people react much as you think they would. Picture how Donald Trump would react to people bursting into flame and how he would deal with those infected, in an effort to quell the disease.That's exactly what happens here. Hatred and fear of infection takes over and leads to even more deaths-most of which were unnecessary.<br /><br />I'm a big fan of Joe Hill and when I heard about this book, I went about making it my life's mission to get an advance copy and I'm so glad I did. The Fireman is, in my opinion, his best book yet. The characters are the most developed we've seen from him so far, which makes it difficult to witness the trials Hill puts them through.<br /> <br />Mr. Hill excels at writing extremely strong women and Harper is no exception. She is a nurse who willingly helps treat those with the 'scale, while many in the medical field, and her own husband, want to run headlong in the opposite direction. Turns out Harper's husband is nothing like what she thought he was, and when she, herself, becomes infected, he makes it out to be her fault, and his true self is finally revealed. Fighting the disease, fighting her husband, trying to fight against the spread of the 'scale, Harper is a true hero and she owns this story. <br /> <br />Populated with other strong characters, both good and bad, this story reflects an imagination with a broad scope and a penchant for suffering. Although, at times Hill's prose rambles, I never found myself bored or losing interest; only becoming more agitated, worried and excited about what was going to come next. Would Harper make it through this? What about the plucky survivors, both good and evil? What about her horrible husband? You'll have to read this book to find out!<br /> <br />The Fireman was an epic tale, populated with characters you love and hate, highlighting what's both good and bad in society today. Somehow, though, I came out of the experience with a sense of hope and also a sense of excitement regarding what Joe Hill will do next. <br /> <br />Highly recommended for fans of post- apocalyptic tales and fans of Joe Hill!<br /> <br />*Thanks to the publisher and Edelweiss for providing a free e-ARC of The Fireman in exchange for an honest review. This is it!*<br /> <br /> <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6428381898739353430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1832196025" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1832196025" />
    <a title="Ginger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger"><img alt="Ginger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593449448p2/14097149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1832196025?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginger" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger">Ginger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26222107-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1832196025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7426096528951111809">Wow! I’m glad I read this when I did. It seems everyone has read <b>The Fireman</b>.<br/>I didn’t go into this book expecting much due to mixed reviews.<br/><br/>I love <i>Joe Hill</i>’s writing because he loves short chapters and well thought out plots. His imagination is fantastic and I’m always excited to read another book by him.<br/>Because of the mixed reviews on <b>The Fireman</b>, it brought down my expectations a bit. <br/><br/>Maybe that’s why I liked it so much! I went into this book neutral.<br/><br/><b>The Fireman</b> starts off with the world liter</span>
  <span id="freeText7426096528951111809" style="display:none">Wow! I’m glad I read this when I did. It seems everyone has read <b>The Fireman</b>.<br />I didn’t go into this book expecting much due to mixed reviews.<br /><br />I love <i>Joe Hill</i>’s writing because he loves short chapters and well thought out plots. His imagination is fantastic and I’m always excited to read another book by him.<br />Because of the mixed reviews on <b>The Fireman</b>, it brought down my expectations a bit. <br /><br />Maybe that’s why I liked it so much! I went into this book neutral.<br /><br /><b>The Fireman</b> starts off with the world literally burning to death. The human race has been infected with Draco Incendia Trychophyton. It’s a highly contagious and deadly spore that causes people to burst into flames. Not much is known about the disease except that it marks people with beautiful black and gold marks across their bodies. If you’re infected with “Dragonscale”, you’re unable to hide it.<br /><br /><b>My only complaint:</b><br /><br /><b>The Fireman</b> felt a bit too much like <b>The Stand</b> with some of the characters. A little boy named Nick who was deaf, unlikeable Harold Cross and the “pregnant” Frannie, uh I mean Harper.<br />So yeah, the characters and descriptions of them were REALLY waaaaay too similar in my opinion.<br /><br />Maybe <i>Joe Hill</i> was writing a love letter to his dad’s famous book?<br />Honestly, I’m mixed on it. I like both books!<br />I liked that he did it and at the same time, felt like it was a bit “too much”.<br />Other than that, that’s the only thing that I can bitch about with this book.<br /><br /><b>Things that I liked:</b><br /><br />The characters (lots to love and also HATE), the action and tension that keeps building.<br />I loved the unsettling moments of horde mentality and cult-like actions that were going down in Camp Wyndham.<br />I loved how the book shows civilized society breaking down with cremation crews along with the overall stupidity and fear of not understanding something.<br /><i>Joe Hill</i> does really well showing this to the readers in <b>The Fireman</b>! He really racks up the tense and crazy in this book!<br /><br />If you want to see society collapse, introduce Dragonscale to the world and just watch it ignite in hate, fear, crazy propaganda and misinformation.<br />I would definitely recommend this book if you’re into post apocalyptic themes!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7426096528951111809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1702284941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1702284941" />
    <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda"><img alt="Arah-Lynda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601299926p2/5859453.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1702284941?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arah-Lynda" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda">Arah-Lynda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062440235" href="/book/show/26029517-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5859453-arah-lynda?shelf=i-said">i-said</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1702284941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9827573431905142895">By Jove, reading this was as much fun as a laundry basket full of curious kittens. It is a virtual treasure trove of pop culture references, a tip of the hat if you will to J.K. Rowling, George R.R. Martin and of course his father, plus many, many more, not the least of which is Mary Poppins. Be careful where you step as you will find yourself tripping over them during the course of your reading experience. Such fun!<br/><br/>Okay so first the premise:<br/><br/>A plague of sorts is sweeping across the civilized wor</span>
  <span id="freeText9827573431905142895" style="display:none">By Jove, reading this was as much fun as a laundry basket full of curious kittens. It is a virtual treasure trove of pop culture references, a tip of the hat if you will to J.K. Rowling, George R.R. Martin and of course his father, plus many, many more, not the least of which is Mary Poppins. Be careful where you step as you will find yourself tripping over them during the course of your reading experience. Such fun!<br /><br />Okay so first the premise:<br /><br />A plague of sorts is sweeping across the civilized world. Its proper scientific name is Draco Incendia Trychophyton but it is more commonly referred to as Dragonscale. It is highly contagious, marking its victims with black and gold scroll like marks across their bodies before they eventually burst into flames and are devoured by fire. Once infected there does not appear to be a cure and no one is entirely sure how it is spread from one person to another causing wide spread panic and the inhumane treatment of those showing signs of infection.<br /><br />Harper Grayson, our protagonist, is a nurse working at a local hospital when she first meets The Fireman and assists him, against the odds and hospital protocol, in getting timely medical care to a young boy in his care suffering from abdominal distress. Shortly after finishing her stint at the hospital she learns that she is expecting. On the heels of this happy news Harper sees the tell tale marks of the Dragonscale upon her own body. Her husband is convinced that Harper brought this plague upon herself and no doubt him as well, as a result of her work at the hospital. He is incensed and things do not go well between them. <br /><br />Now Harper is running for her life and that of her unborn child. But The Fireman does not soon forget past kindnesses and steps in to rescue her from her murderous husband. The Fireman it would seem can control the fire burning beneath his Dragonscale and use it as a weapon against those that wish him and others harm. He delivers Harper safely to a backwoods summer camp called Camp Wynward, where the residents have found a ritual that keeps the flames of spontaneous combustion at bay. <br /><br />But the world around them is in chaos and there are Cremation Squads out there determined to stop this fiery spore by eliminating all those infected. <br /><br /><br /><blockquote>You had a hold on me<br />Right from the start<br />A grip so tight <br />I couldn't tear it apart<br />My nerves all jumpin' <br />Actin' like a fool<br />Well your kisses they burn <br />But your heart stays cool</blockquote><br /><blockquote>The Boss</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><br />If you are a young aspiring writer and your father just happens to be Stephen King, well let’s just say those are some mighty big boots to fill. Joe Hill tackles this challenge head on and make no mistake he is getting better and better. <br /><br /><br />If you are looking for an entertaining summer read that demands little, beyond suspension of belief, and delivers a few chuckles along the way, then by all means pick up this high octane thriller. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9827573431905142895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1748163685" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1748163685" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1748163685?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062200631" href="/book/show/25816688-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=big-tomes">big-tomes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1748163685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1412543927481093875">Joe Hill's last novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/625662512?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>NOS4A2</a> was an engaging horror romp which lasted for more than seven hundred pages, but maintained to keep both tension and interest in the reader to the very end. In comparison, Hill's latest novel is completely unlike its predecessor, with whom it only shares its enormous length. To put it simply - <i>The Fireman</i> is an overly long, convoluted, uninteresting and ultimately very disappointing effort.<br/><br/>At its heart, <i>The Fireman</i> is a post-apocalyptic novel, with a premise that has</span>
  <span id="freeText1412543927481093875" style="display:none">Joe Hill's last novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/625662512?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">NOS4A2</a> was an engaging horror romp which lasted for more than seven hundred pages, but maintained to keep both tension and interest in the reader to the very end. In comparison, Hill's latest novel is completely unlike its predecessor, with whom it only shares its enormous length. To put it simply - <i>The Fireman</i> is an overly long, convoluted, uninteresting and ultimately very disappointing effort.<br /><br />At its heart, <i>The Fireman</i> is a post-apocalyptic novel, with a premise that has by now been done hundreds of times: the majority of humanity is inflicted by a ravaging disease, leaving only a small group of survivors trying to scrape by. This time humanity is afflicted by a disease which becomes known as Dragonscale - its symptoms include dark marks on the skin, which spread across the body and eventually cause the individual to literally erupt into flames and burn to death. Dragonscale spreads rapidly, and soon consumes millions of people - as well as the environment, causing uncontrollable forest fires and so on. Although the demise of humanity is not a new theme, you have to give it to <i>The Fireman</i> - it is probably the world's first novel about human extinction by spontaneous combustion.<br /><br />The problem with the book is that not much else about it is new, or even particularly interesting. As we read the <i>The Fireman</i>, we get the sense of crossing through familiar territory - one which has been done many times before, and much better so. Since every post-apocalyptic story requires a bunch of survivors, we find ourselves in a tight spot. Consider this - how does one escape a disease which literally consumes human bodies and turns them to ash? Easily - by learning how to not be unharmed by it. And not only that - it turns out that you can learn how to control the disease and <i>use it to your advantage</i>.<br /><br />That's right. The disease kills most of humanity, but luckily for a selected number of people - who happen to be the characters which the book focuses on - it can also provide handy superpowers. Joe Hill said at a panel that his book would be "less like Matheson, and more like Crichton" and cited Crichton's first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7670.The_Andromeda_Strain" title="The Andromeda Strain by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">The Andromeda Strain</a> as an example. The only link with Michael Crichton that I can find in this book is Joe Hill's attempt at quasi-scientific explanation of Dragonscale and how it affects human bodies - something which he later totally throws out of the window by essentially allowing several characters to overcome its malicious effect by their own feelings, as apparently this is all what it takes (and somehow we have to believe these same characters never thought about broadcasting their solution to the problem to the entire world, but then again if they did we would not have a book to read and review).<br /><br />As I mentioned, people in this book not only escape death by learning to coexist with a disease that should burn them to death, but also learn how to control it and use it to their advantage. This means that later in the book characters in the book are able to generate fire literally from their fingertips, control and shape it - throw fireballs and whatnot, or in case of one character create creatures made of fire. This is why the supposed inspiration by Michael Crichton was so puzzling - Crichton was a writer interested in science and technology, famed for his research and the ability to plausibly convey and explain his theories, and would not employ a purely fantastical cop-out as a solution to them. What made his books interesting was not his prose style , or the depth of his characters- he was a passable writer at best, and his characters are forgettable cardboard cutouts - or even in most cases the story itself, which usually consisted of little more than a bunch of frenetic action sequences. What made Crichton's novels so interesting were the ideas within them, which usually focused on mankind's technological progress and the way it affects our life and society. Usually, Crichton would have his characters engage in long discussions about the nature of what they were experiencing - its moral, ethical and scientific implications - and these formed the most interesting part of the book; it is especially evident in books such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/455373.Sphere" title="Sphere by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Sphere</a>, which is probably his best novel.<br /><br />This is precisely what <i>The Fireman</i> lacks - any kind of complexity, something to chew on, somethink would give readers a lot to think about. This is a novel which does not give any answers except the most obvious ones, and does not ask any questions. Its characters are very forgettable and barely, and there is no real reason to care about any of them. Even the eponymous character, en English guy who wears a fireman's suit and is henceforth nicknamed "The Fireman" is little more than a convenient plot device to rescue our protagonists in their moments of trouble - he rarely makes an appearance throughout most of the book until the very end, and spends most of his time hiding away in a remote cabin. Interactions between these characters are boring and simply unimaginative, including what is probably a most ham-fisted romantic relationship written in recent fiction. Poorly designed characters who do not grow as people hurt the book twice, as they make it hard for us to care about the story, since it is difficult to care for what these uninteresting people experience. Because why should we?<br /><br />Not that the story itself is complex and interesting; it really is not, and the vast majority of it reminds me of a very (pardon the pun) watered down version of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/149267.The_Stand" title="The Stand by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stand</a>. It is darkly ironic that Joe Hill began writing under a pseudonym because he wanted to escape his father's shadow, yet in this book he falls completely under it. <i>The Fireman</i> features all of the classic Stephen King tropes - the constant foreshadowing at the end of the chapter (in the vein of "it was a good plan, until everything blew up", "he never saw her again), many references to popular culture, endless references to music that the author likes (which sound completely unbelievable when put into minds of the characters many years younger - how many 26 year olds think about the difference between The Rolling Stones and the Beatles?), a crazed sociopath ex-husband/lover, crazy religious woman leader who seems to find her way here from <i>The Mist</i>...there is even an unsympathetic character named <b>Harold</b> who is almost a carbon copy of his namesake from <i>The Stand</i>, not to mention a mute character named <b>Nick</b> who is the epitome of innocence and good, just like the mute <b>Nick</b> from <i>The Stand</i>. All this can be explained as a homage or an Easter egg, of course, but if the book features little else than homages and Easter eggs, what is left? Not much.<br /><br />Yes, despite all this, <i>The Fireman</i> is the longest of all of Joe Hill's novels so far, and perhaps his most disappointing ones. Its length is in no way justified, and feels padded to the bone; I do not think I exaggerate when I say that you could skip entire chapters and not miss out on much, if anything. It reads well and fast, since Joe Hill is a good and able writer, but there is little point in reading most of it. There is nothing enlightening or innovative in this book; neither the story or the characters are deep enough to become memorable and worth revisiting. For a novel focused on the element of fire, it inexplicably lacks the spark to keep the flame going; and it eventually goes out, quietly and without much smoke. I have given the book two stars only because of my sympathy for its author, and because it is not completely terrible - but it definitely is uninspired, unimaginative, uninteresting and definitely unworthy of your time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1412543927481093875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1436182462" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1436182462" />
    <a title="Chris " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1956959-chris"><img alt="Chris " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502408626p2/1956959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1436182462?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062200631" href="/book/show/25816688-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=read-owned-hardcover">read-owned-hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=specfic-group-reads">specfic-group-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1436182462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4485526745368147187">So I've read all of Joe Hill's books (other than some rare stories and some of the comics), and of course when <i>The Fireman</i> came out I had to get a copy immediately. It did take me a few months to get to it. I didn't know what it was about, except that it had something to do with a fireman. But I trust Joe Hill and he hasn't let me down yet.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482472947ra/21520448.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So right away we were seeing that something was very wrong. The apocalypse was nigh, as we learned pretty early on that some dreaded disease was sweeping acro</span>
  <span id="freeText4485526745368147187" style="display:none">So I've read all of Joe Hill's books (other than some rare stories and some of the comics), and of course when <i>The Fireman</i> came out I had to get a copy immediately. It did take me a few months to get to it. I didn't know what it was about, except that it had something to do with a fireman. But I trust Joe Hill and he hasn't let me down yet.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482472947ra/21520448.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So right away we were seeing that something was very wrong. The apocalypse was nigh, as we learned pretty early on that some dreaded disease was sweeping across America and Canada. Something called Dragonscale, which caused scaly marks to form on the skin. Sometimes they would smoke, and the victims would quite frequently burst into spontaneous infernos.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482473452ra/21520473.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The pacing of this book is a comfortable, slow burn. It's really easy to sink in and become attached to the characters and their situations. It reminds me in several places of Stephen King's <i>The Stand</i>, though focused on a smaller group of point of view characters. I often suspected that these similarities were intentional as homage to King's book (and other works), as well as to other apocalyptic themed authors and stories. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482473105ra/21520452.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've found that it's very difficult to write a review for a book like this, one that packs so much heat in just over 700 pages. I don't want to give away any spoilers, so it's hard to go into the story that much. I will say that I love the main character, Harper, as she adapts to the changes in her life and the world she's forced to survive in. That being said, her story and that of the supporting characters, is highly recommended. As the winter sinks in, it might even help warm things up for a bit...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482473954ra/21520489.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>

<div id="review_1423365989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423365989" />
    <a title="Paul O&#39;Neill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17331573-paul-o-neill"><img alt="Paul O&#39;Neill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462480730p2/17331573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1423365989?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul O&#39;Neill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul O&#39;Neill" href="/user/show/17331573-paul-o-neill">Paul O&#39;Neill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575130722" href="/book/show/25994058-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1423365989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5047463834983964833"><i>Awesome book. I expect no less from one of my favourite authors</i><br/><br/>Whilst entirely different to his other works, this still hits the mark. Less of his trademark horror (although he does a good job of creating terror and suspense when required) but not quite the stereotypical post-apocalyptic story we've all become used to. <br/><br/>The conditions that cause this story to unfold are all very well thought out. Harper, our main character, has to be up there with one of the best characters I've read (I was going</span>
  <span id="freeText5047463834983964833" style="display:none"><i>Awesome book. I expect no less from one of my favourite authors</i><br /><br />Whilst entirely different to his other works, this still hits the mark. Less of his trademark horror (although he does a good job of creating terror and suspense when required) but not quite the stereotypical post-apocalyptic story we've all become used to. <br /><br />The conditions that cause this story to unfold are all very well thought out. Harper, our main character, has to be up there with one of the best characters I've read (I was going to qualify that as one of the best female characters I've ever read but I think she's one of the best overall, male, female, dragons, robot, all). <br /><br />Hill's writing style is perfect in my view. Very easy to digest, never any long waffling exposition or needless information. The story flows very nicely and chapter size is perfect. <br /><br />Highly recommended for all Hill fans. <br /><br />I did, however, have a couple of very minor gripes with it. Not nearly enough to knock it down a star but two things that irritated me (I'm nitpicking but thought they are worth calling out as it would be interesting to find out if anyone feels the same). <br /><br />1 - Comparisons to the Stand were always going to happen. His dad wrote my favourite book. Whilst I think it's cool that Hill gave minor nods to his dad's works in NOS4R2 (and maybe others I can't remember), he did it a bit too much here. In the Fireman we have:<br />A deaf person called Nick<br />A person called Harold Cross - who keeps a diary<br />A Frannie<br />A pregnancy<br />And probably a few others I can't quite remember<br /><br />It's not a huge problem, I just didn't want to be reminded of the greatest post apocalyptic book of all time whilst reading a post apocalyptic book. <br /><br />2 - This one is a bigger problem and one I want to get your thought on, as King does it in a few of his novels and I'm sure there are others. I refer to a spoiler sentence right at the end of a chapter. As in:<br /><i>but that was the last time he was seen alive</i><br /><i>but when they returned, everything will have changed forever</i><br />Etc.<br /><br />Anybody else get really annoyed by this? You're going to kill someone in the next chapter so let me feel the shock of it happening as it happens in the story. Don't take the impact away from me in a sentence. To be fair, the Fireman isn't nearly as bad for this. It does it a few times but it still irks me. <br /><br />Minor moans aside, you should read this and Hill remains on my automatic buy list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5047463834983964833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1551526008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1551526008" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jay" href="/user/show/10633920-jay">Jay</a>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10633920-jay?shelf=edelweiss-arc">edelweiss-arc</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1551526008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15683401312786566379">Holy fuck. This book.....<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456347766ra/18222713.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>WAS OUT OF THIS WORLD AMAZING!!!</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456347876ra/18222717.gif' alt='excited cat photo 1310247277001.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Spoilers marked in review :)<br/><br/>I was a little nervous about starting <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20927079.The_Fireman' title='The Fireman by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fireman</a> because of how long it was. I often find that books more than ~400 pages have a tendency to feel diluted and I usually end up skim-reading or skipping entire pages. <br/><br/><b>If anything, I wished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20927079.The_Fireman' title='The Fireman by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fireman</a> was longer than 768 pages.</b><br/><br/>A deadly pandemic sweeps across the globe, infecting people with <i>Draco Incendia Trychophyton</i>, aka <b>Dragonscale</b>. It marks the hosts with black</span>
  <span id="freeText15683401312786566379" style="display:none">Holy fuck. This book.....<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456347766ra/18222713.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>WAS OUT OF THIS WORLD AMAZING!!!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456347876ra/18222717.gif" alt="excited cat photo 1310247277001.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Spoilers marked in review :)<br><br>I was a little nervous about starting <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20927079.The_Fireman" title="The Fireman by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fireman</a> because of how long it was. I often find that books more than ~400 pages have a tendency to feel diluted and I usually end up skim-reading or skipping entire pages. <br><br><b>If anything, I wished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20927079.The_Fireman" title="The Fireman by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fireman</a> was longer than 768 pages.</b><br><br>A deadly pandemic sweeps across the globe, infecting people with <i>Draco Incendia Trychophyton</i>, aka <b>Dragonscale</b>. It marks the hosts with black and gold marks all over their body before making them spontaneously combust. <br><br>Some people start off by smoking a little...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456354573i/18223286._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>.... while others catch on fire without any warning.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456348971ra/18222839.gif" width="200" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Harper, our main character, is a nurse in this increasingly <s>fucked</s> messed up world who discovers the marks on her own body.... straight after finding out she's pregnant. I found this really cool - a person suddenly gifted with new signs of life and death. From the synopsis, you probably already know that douchebag hubby, Jakob, loses it a little when Harper decides to live for the baby instead of killing herself with him. <br><br>I personally <b>ADORED</b> Harper. She was independent, brave, smart, kind, witty and tough. She felt very real and there was none of that Mary Sue/Martyr Complex/Choosen One bullshit that is so popular in books today. I think Harper reminded me of Claire from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10964.Outlander__Outlander___1_" title="Outlander (Outlander, #1) by Diana Gabaldon" rel="nofollow noopener">Outlander</a>.<br><br>Now enter The Fireman. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456357019i/18223518.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While the rest of the world is all:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456357276ra/18223625.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He's more:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456357276ra/18223626.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved him too! He was a little cocky, very cheeky, and extremely down to earth. <br><br>I did consider giving it 4 stars for a couple of reasons:<br><br><b>1 - </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The book's title is "The Fireman" but he spends the majority of the book on his little island, recovering from injuries. I missed him having a more active role in the story. I mean, Harper was an awesome character to follow but I wanted to see more of John. He also lost a lot of that enigma he had in the beginning.<br><br>He wasn't a real fireman either! :(  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>2 - </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I found it a little weird how they were confessing their love for each other even though the Fireman was still keeping his dead ex's "fire spirit" (or whatever you want to call it) around. He kept risking everyone's life for some enchanted coal and it was completely out of character for Harper to be even mildly okay with that. I kind of missed their chemistry towards the end as well. They got together but I didn't really get excited over it as much as I usually do when two people I'm rooting for end up together. Maybe it was a little hurried for me?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>3 - </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was a little disappointed that Hill didn't play with the fire aspect more. I think it would have been really cool if he made it a little more... Avatar-esque:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457183519ra/18329619.gif" width="200" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457184007ra/18329735.gif" width="200" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457184008ra/18329736.gif" width="200" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457184256ra/18329836.gif" width="200" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>4 - (biggest spoiler that you should stay away from if you have not read the book) </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[WHYYYYYY DID HE HAVE TO DIIIIIEEEEEEEEE? WHY. WHY. WHY. WHY. WHY. I actually shed a tear or two. WHHHHHYYYYYYYYYY  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>So yes, I had a couple of problems with it but overall, this book was absolutely fantastic. Every character was expertly developed, the story was well paced and MY. GOD. Joe Hill can write! I'm totally blown away. There's honestly nothing else on my mind right now. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20927079.The_Fireman" title="The Fireman by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fireman</a> should have a warning on it instructing readers not to drive a motor vehicle or operate heavy machinery for a day or two after finishing the book.<br><br><b>10/10 would recommend.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395187687ra/8962944.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Thank you so much Edelweiss and William Morrow Publishing for this ARC :)</i><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1526773120" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1526773120" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1526773120?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062200655" href="/book/show/20927079-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=reading-envy-podcast">reading-envy-podcast</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2016">read2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=reviewcopy">reviewcopy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1526773120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13104613417001289595">This is a perfect book. I downloaded the review copy with a bit of trepidation - the length, the genre - I read it, devoured it, in two days. 200 pages on Saturday and 513 pages on Sunday. The pacing is perfect and the occasional humor makes for a very enjoyable read.<br/><br/>Dragonscale is a sickness that is highly contagious and can cause people to spontaneously combust. Half the world is burning down and people with Dragonscale are being hunted before they can infect others. Harper is a nurse who is t</span>
  <span id="freeText13104613417001289595" style="display:none">This is a perfect book. I downloaded the review copy with a bit of trepidation - the length, the genre - I read it, devoured it, in two days. 200 pages on Saturday and 513 pages on Sunday. The pacing is perfect and the occasional humor makes for a very enjoyable read.<br /><br />Dragonscale is a sickness that is highly contagious and can cause people to spontaneously combust. Half the world is burning down and people with Dragonscale are being hunted before they can infect others. Harper is a nurse who is treating people at a local hospital, where she meets a few unusual characters - Reneé, the volunteer who walks out the door one day, completely lit up from the inside but not burning; The Fireman, who brings in a little boy needing surgery. When that hospital burns down and her husband turns into a crazy person, Harper seeks out a community of others suffering from Dragonscale.<br /><br />This is where the book could have started to feel like other apocalypse/disaster novels, and in some ways it does - cultish community, people turning insane with power, weird religions - but these are the things I love about apocalypse books. But the choices that are made and the very unique properties of Dragonscale keep it interesting. <br /><br />Dragonscale also may be a metaphor <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ - the community survives and thrives even with Dragonscale when they are united, but sometimes they are united for the wrong purpose... I did find myself thinking about the similarities in politics and religion in our current society. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This book was discussed on <a href="http://readingenvy.blogspot.com/2016/08/reading-envy-065-creeping-through.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Episode 065</a> of the Reading Envy Podcast.<br /><br />The one downside to having a review copy is that I can't put little quotes that made me laugh here in this review, but when I buy the book for myself, I'll come back.<br /><br /><i>I was provided a review copy of this book from the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review. I appreciate the chance because I had yet to read a novel by Joe Hill, and was surprised at how much I liked it.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13104613417001289595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8575414-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441431450p2/8575414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1643403541?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/8575414-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1643403541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14147206764546622248">Joe Hill, what have you gone and done?! I have been waiting a long time for your new book to be published and then you went and made it so good that I couldn't put it down and now I've finished it! That was quite a trip.<br/><br/>Joe Hill has total mastery of this story. His writing is witty and his cultural referencing is spot on. There are many references to Harry Potter (he must be a child of the generation who grew up reading those volumes) and to his dad's works, John Grisham and of course Mary Poppi</span>
  <span id="freeText14147206764546622248" style="display:none">Joe Hill, what have you gone and done?! I have been waiting a long time for your new book to be published and then you went and made it so good that I couldn't put it down and now I've finished it! That was quite a trip.<br /><br />Joe Hill has total mastery of this story. His writing is witty and his cultural referencing is spot on. There are many references to Harry Potter (he must be a child of the generation who grew up reading those volumes) and to his dad's works, John Grisham and of course Mary Poppins.<br />'Just because you've read John Grisham, it doesn't make you a Supreme Court Justice'.<br /><br />Hill has created a cast of flawed and fascinating individuals and managed to come up with a main character, Harper, who was perfectly balanced : while often compared to and quoting Mary Poppins and Julie Andrews, she still managed to avoid being a Mary Poppins character.<br /><br />And as a study of people and the psychology of human kind, we see the Lord of the Flies-esque take on how we behave under peer group pressure and how we thrive on approval, whatever the cost. 'Law is whoever is holding the nightstick' some one observes at one point.<br /><br />Hill has a great way of ending most chapters that leads you right on to the next one and the next. until you end up finishing it too soon and having a long old wait for the next book by this author. Which is where I came in with this review and a good place to finish!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14147206764546622248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2103016938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2103016938" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598060221p2/2172096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2103016938?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>
