        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2103016938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10397658964949267450"><br/><br/>A horrible malady is spreading like wildfire through the human population. Caused by spores from a fungus called Draco Incendia Trychophyton.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592950i/29976346.png' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The illness - named Dragonscale - is manifested by gold and black scales on the skin. On the upside, the scales are rather pretty and decorative.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592950i/29976347.png' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>On the downside, they cause victims to spontaneously combust.....to suddenly burst into flames and incinerate. And there's no treatment or cure.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592950i/29976348.png' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Harper Grayson is a twenty-something nurse who's tending to Dragonscal</span>
  <span id="freeText10397658964949267450" style="display:none"><br><br>A horrible malady is spreading like wildfire through the human population. Caused by spores from a fungus called Draco Incendia Trychophyton.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592950i/29976346.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The illness - named Dragonscale - is manifested by gold and black scales on the skin. On the upside, the scales are rather pretty and decorative.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592950i/29976347.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>On the downside, they cause victims to spontaneously combust.....to suddenly burst into flames and incinerate. And there's no treatment or cure.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592950i/29976348.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Harper Grayson is a twenty-something nurse who's tending to Dragonscale patients in Maine's Portsmouth Hospital. Like other caregivers, Harper wears a protective rubber suit to shield her from the spores. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976349.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One day a fireman carries an ailing boy into the hospital, and Harper - suspecting the child has appendicitis - helps them jump the line to get help. This turns out to be a pivotal event in the nurse's life.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976350.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Despite her precautions, Harper starts to see gold and black streaks on her skin.....and knows she's doomed. The nurse has an added concern, however. She recently got pregnant and desperately wants to see her baby born, in the belief that fetuses don't contract Dragonscale from their mothers.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976351.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Harper's husband, Jakob, sees her Dragonscale marks, he's enraged. He blames Harper for bringing the illness into their home and - afraid of being infected - takes off.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976352.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Harper quarantines herself in the house, but is running out of food and supplies when Jakob suddenly returns - with a gun. He thinks he has Dragonscale, and plans to kill Harper and himself before they spontaneously combust.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976353.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Harper escapes from Jakob and is rescued by the fireman (a British man whose name is John Rookwood), a teenage girl, and the boy from the hospital - who happens to be deaf. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976354.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The trio leads Harper to an out-of-the-way enclave called Camp Wyndham, which houses a secret community of Dragonscale victims. The group, led by a man called Father Story, has learned to tame the disease.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976355.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>According to Father Story, 'if you create a feeling of security, the Dragonscale lives in harmony with you'.....and you don't burn to death. The people at Camp Wyndham attend services every day, where they sing together. This engenders a peaceful feeling that makes the people glow - a condition called 'The Bright.' And one spore-carrier, John Rookwood, has even learned to ignite parts of himself - with no permanent damage. This is a formidable weapon when the fireman needs one!<br><br>Most of the story is set at Camp Wyndham, which contains a variety of inhabitants - some good, some bad. I don't want to give away too much of the plot, but I will say that, in time, the community gets a new leader and becomes a kind of dictatorship - with harsh, medieval punishments for people who break the rules.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976356.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In part, this is to ensure the residents' safety. The outside world has gone crazy, and rogue 'cremation squads' make it their business to hunt down and shoot Dragonscale victims - who they call burners. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976357.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jakob has become an ardent member of an assassination crew and is determined to kill his wife, among others. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976358.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are some exciting, action-packed scenes where kill squads meet up with burners.<br><br>As in any community, love sometimes blooms in Camp Wyndham. Harper and Rookwood are attracted to each other, but - for various reasons - their relationship is very complicated. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976359.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Another couple bonds as well - two people who'd probably never meet in the real world. It's all very sweet.....and fans of romance novels will probably enjoy these minor plotpoints.<br><br>Harper experiences a host of difficulties in the course of the story, but is driven to survive - at least until she gives birth. The nurse hopes to give the child to a healthy couple to raise. This seems a tall order to me. Who would believe this baby wasn't infected? I understand a mother's hopes though, and the drive to reproduce.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976360.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"The Fireman" - in which a community of 'survivors' is divided into 'good' and 'evil' factions - was clearly influenced by Stephen King's book "The Stand." This isn't a surprise, since King is the author's father.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597592951i/29976361.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Still, "The Fireman" is very original in its chosen catastrophe - an illness that causes spontaneous combustion is certainly unique (and horrifying)! And the story plays out much differently than The Stand.<br><br>There are a lot of interesting characters in the book, including: a delusional leader who wants to maintain total control; acolytes who'll do anything to please the boss; a man on the side of the angels; chauvinist burner-bashers who think they can do whatever they please; a sweet orphan who longs for a mother; bullying teenage girls; hormonal teenage boys; escaped convicts; and more.<br><br>The book is perhaps a bit overlong, but the story moves along at a good clip and held my attention. The tale has many references to popular culture, including: well-known celebrities and politicians (many of whom go up in flames); Mary Poppins; Harry Potter; and others. These were fun and added a touch of humor to the story. I had an idea about what would happen at the climax - and I was right - but this didn't diminish my enjoyment of the book.<br><br>Very good horror/thriller, highly recommended to fans of the genre.<br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot....</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10397658964949267450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1505977208" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1505977208" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1505977208?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062565334" href="/book/show/29100336-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1505977208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8174536622358157372">I just realized that it took me almost a month to finish this novel. I read the whole ASOIF series in a span of about 25 days, meaning about 5 days each for a 1000+ page novel. This novel is only 700+ pages long but I didn't finish it soon enough. I can blame my busy schedule or my occasional lack of interest to read, but honestly, the novel has a lot of weak spots.<br/><br/>I read NOS4R2 by the same author and I didn't like the book that much. When I read about this book though, I was completely stoked a</span>
  <span id="freeText8174536622358157372" style="display:none">I just realized that it took me almost a month to finish this novel. I read the whole ASOIF series in a span of about 25 days, meaning about 5 days each for a 1000+ page novel. This novel is only 700+ pages long but I didn't finish it soon enough. I can blame my busy schedule or my occasional lack of interest to read, but honestly, the novel has a lot of weak spots.<br /><br />I read NOS4R2 by the same author and I didn't like the book that much. When I read about this book though, I was completely stoked and bought the novel as soon as I saw it at my local bookstore. I read it the same day that I bought it, but sadly it didn't take me that fast to finish it. While I enjoyed this a lot more than NOS4R2, I'm still honestly a bit disappointed. Hill still hasn't wow-ed me, but hopefully the third novel would be the charm. <br /><br />The novel has a lot of fillers and it could've been 200 pages shorter. The first 1/3 of the novel really had me at the edge of my seat, but then the middle slacked off. Then the middle started to become interesting, then it started to slack off again. Then it became interesting again not until about 75% in the novel. The novel is highly inconsistent, and sadly that really affected my reading mood.<br /><br />While the plot is inconsistent as hell, thankfully the characters made up for that huge flaw. I really liked almost all of them. I hated Allie at first, but I learned to like her in the end. Harper is your typical neutral protagonist who tries to be a hero, but doesn't really qualify to be one. John is honestly both the strong and weak point when it comes to the characters. While he is interesting and plays a huge role in the novel, he is as inconsistent as the plot. The antagonists are also interesting, especially Jakob. Carol on the other hand really annoyed me. I wanted her gone a few paragraphs in. <br /><br />The Sci-Fi aspect of the novel really stood out in my opinion. I understood most of the things that Hill incorporated because I studied mycology just a few months ago. I know that this new fungal species that Hill created is clearly fictional, it still entertained me. The apocalyptic aspect of the novel resembles some novels I've read before, but overall for me it can be considered original. It's not one of those annoying sci-fi/apocalypse that are really predictable and laughable.<br /><br />I was really confused as to whether this novel deserves a 3 or 4 star rating, but I had already established that it clearly deserves a 3.5 rating. This is one of the reason why Goodreads really needs to add the half star option. I opted to rate this novel 4 stars because while there are a bunch of bad parts, the entire novel is really interesting and commendable. The characters would leave you yearning for more, and honestly the ending did not satisfy my curiosity. A bunch of short stories might help with my curiosity, but it seems like Hill wanted this to be a standalone. I'm not particularly happy with the ending because it has a lot of loopholes that Hill didn't really fix. I think maybe he opted for an open-ended novel, but I'm not happy with it.<br /><br />If you're a Sci-Fi fan and really likes novels that heavily depend on the premise and the characters to make it interesting, then this is for you. I myself forgave the author for the boring parts, and I'm sure that you guys can too. I know it seems that a 4 star rating is too high for a novel that I didn't really enjoy, I'm honestly still recommending this. It's too long, but still fun overall. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8174536622358157372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1642591268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer728158270930844102">Now this is what I call a GOOD book. In fact it is a brilliant book especially if, like me, you have a liking for dystopian stories. You could say that it is yet another story in which the world is being ravaged by a plague of some kind, which is killing people off in their millions. That is exactly what happens but the "plague" in this case is fresh from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/88506.Joe_Hill' title='Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>Joe Hill</a>'s vivid imagination and it is totally original and very cleverly done.<br/>The fireman of the title is a wonderful character - an ordinary</span>
  <span id="freeText728158270930844102" style="display:none">Now this is what I call a GOOD book. In fact it is a brilliant book especially if, like me, you have a liking for dystopian stories. You could say that it is yet another story in which the world is being ravaged by a plague of some kind, which is killing people off in their millions. That is exactly what happens but the "plague" in this case is fresh from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/88506.Joe_Hill" title="Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Joe Hill</a>'s vivid imagination and it is totally original and very cleverly done.<br />The fireman of the title is a wonderful character - an ordinary man with super powers who does what he can to save his little bit of the world or at least some of the people in it. I loved Harper and Nick and Allie and even Sarah who only really has one scene but it is an amazing one<br />The book is long but I never felt that it faltered. It is a great story with masses of action and pages which practically turn themselves. Loved it.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1647024666" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1647024666" />
    <a title="Kandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice"><img alt="Kandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1647024666?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandice" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice">Kandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062200631" href="/book/show/25816688-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1647024666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14412388042726024144">What a read! Seriously, this is not at all what I was expecting. I have come to expect a certain bit of gore from Mr. Hill and this book had almost none. I’m not saying it was an easy read. It wasn’t. It’s basically an apocolyptic novel so who could expect happiness and light? Keeping in mind the topic and Hill’s other novels, if you were looking for a sweet story you have a screw loose. Or two.<br/><br/>The world has been overcome by a devastating plague. What the symptoms are makes no never mind, the fa</span>
  <span id="freeText14412388042726024144" style="display:none">What a read! Seriously, this is not at all what I was expecting. I have come to expect a certain bit of gore from Mr. Hill and this book had almost none. I’m not saying it was an easy read. It wasn’t. It’s basically an apocolyptic novel so who could expect happiness and light? Keeping in mind the topic and Hill’s other novels, if you were looking for a sweet story you have a screw loose. Or two.<br /><br />The world has been overcome by a devastating plague. What the symptoms are makes no never mind, the fact that it is highly contagious and often ends in grisly death is the most important thing about this plague nicknamed “Dragonscale”, or “‘scale” for short. Our protagonist, Harper, is a “look on the bright side” nurse out to save the world. In her efforts she not only contracts “scale", but catches pregnant as well. Talk about rolling snake eyes! We follow Harper through a year of Dragonscale. Hill shows us how one little piece of the world reacts to it and the consequences. <br /><br />I don’t want to summarize the plot because I hate spoiling a good read for others, but trust me, this is a GOOD READ. Hill paints the diseased landscape perfectly. He shows us how the disease is almost beside the point. The real danger is from the other survivors. Not only the other infected, but those left healthy as well. This seems to be the case in most cataclysmic fiction. Much like Kirkman’s The Walking Dead, Hill shows us that the “bad guys” in the situation are often the “good guys” with their masks removed. Hill even goes so far as to use actual masks to drive his point home. Do-gooders wearing masks to remain anonymous and people doing very bad things wearing masks to protect their identity. We wear masks for many different reasons.<br /><br />I was fortunate enough to see Hill recently and he described his reasons and inspirations for this book as society’s reaction to social media. He said when he first stumbled upon Twitter he felt he had found an online home. Now he feels people use it to abuse others anonymously. Not only do we draw strength from online communities comprised of those that share our interests, which was the beauty of Twitter in the early days, but we create mobs by hiding behind their anonymity. We say things online to others we would never say in real life because we are protected not only by our online facelessness, but because it’s easier to go with the group mentality in an online situation. Jump on the band wagon. You aren’t looking at the face of the person you are shaming, bullying or hurting. You are looking at a screen. There is a built in distance. Great concept and very, very true.<br /><br />Back to the actual novel. I grew to genuinely care about the characters, even the characters I disliked, I wanted to know what became of them. I wanted many of them dead, but that still counts as caring about their welfare, right? One of the things I love about Hill’s father, Stephen King, is how he inserts references to his other novels in his writing. He gives you the feeling this is all happening in some other world. Hill does the same here. He makes references to “forgetting the face of her father/mother” which we all know is a recurring Dark Tower theme. It matters not that The Dark Tower is his dad’s world. You think Hill didn’t grow up with it? Of course he did. A character remembers the taste of Nozz A La cola which is another DT reference. That particular reference makes me feel The Fireman may take place in the DT world on a different plane of existence than ours. It could, right? Oh, and Hill also mentions Christmasland, a place of his own design. I love that! <br /><br />I may have started reading Hill because he was his father’s son, but I will keep reading him because he is a terrific writer. I can’t wait for “Strange Weather” to be released next year!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14412388042726024144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1595399904?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/28602001-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26222107-the-fireman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28602001-emma?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1595399904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12380699659141736604">It took me two attempts to read this. That Hill can write is a given. But this book doesn't have any heart. It's not enough of anything to make it memorable. I found myself greeting the ever more depressing and dangerous paths of the plot with little more than a shrug. At the final denouement, I honestly couldn't care less who lived or died. Perhaps because there was little surprise in it, the format of the book was well trodden. Definite points for the creation of Dragonscale, now that was a fu</span>
  <span id="freeText12380699659141736604" style="display:none">It took me two attempts to read this. That Hill can write is a given. But this book doesn't have any heart. It's not enough of anything to make it memorable. I found myself greeting the ever more depressing and dangerous paths of the plot with little more than a shrug. At the final denouement, I honestly couldn't care less who lived or died. Perhaps because there was little surprise in it, the format of the book was well trodden. Definite points for the creation of Dragonscale, now that was a fun change to the usual dystopian fare. <br /><br />I can see why people will love it, but it's far from my favourite of his books. It was too long, too derivative, and too unremarkable outside the one main hook. Still, I felt the same way about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2776789.The_Passage__The_Passage___1_" title="The Passage (The Passage, #1) by Justin Cronin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Passage</a>, which everybody else seemed to love, so what the hell do I know? <br /><br /><br />In any case, thanks to Orion/Gollancz and Netgalley for this copy in exchange for an honest review.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('la2fnji2tnEbqnd0zDOpyO045cyo8cqgnR/f0V3rdoTDzH+YHgk5I5u++tcB3QOxt8iK/duVzSvRZkYcBvOPmw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Rd+pnEs0xPenXLWt9RAK7B/ge0HdqfT5IJ/gUmkc1h0TvkmabYtLpSdIOA44/qCVRRAUcK7N83Js5nmfMgQvAg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/88506.Joe_Hill">About Joe Hill</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/88506.Joe_Hill"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1569331514p3/88506.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/88506.Joe_Hill">Joe Hill
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
20,977
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13271331334091347045">Joe Hill's debut, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153025._Heart_Shaped_Box' title=' Heart-Shaped Box' rel='nofollow noopener'> Heart-Shaped Box</a>, won the Bram Stoker Award for Best First Novel. His second,<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879._Horns' title=' Horns' rel='nofollow noopener'> Horns</a>, was made into a film freakfest starring Daniel Radcliffe. His other novels include <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539._NOS4A2' title=' NOS4A2' rel='nofollow noopener'> NOS4A2</a>, and his #1 New York Times Best-Seller, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25816688._The_Fireman' title=' The Fireman' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Fireman</a>... which was also the winner of a 2016 Goodreads Choice Award for Best Horror Novel.<br/><br/>He writes short stories too. Some of them were gathered together in </span>
  <span id="freeText13271331334091347045" style="display:none">Joe Hill's debut, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153025._Heart_Shaped_Box" title=" Heart-Shaped Box" rel="nofollow noopener"> Heart-Shaped Box</a>, won the Bram Stoker Award for Best First Novel. His second,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879._Horns" title=" Horns" rel="nofollow noopener"> Horns</a>, was made into a film freakfest starring Daniel Radcliffe. His other novels include <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539._NOS4A2" title=" NOS4A2" rel="nofollow noopener"> NOS4A2</a>, and his #1 New York Times Best-Seller, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25816688._The_Fireman" title=" The Fireman" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Fireman</a>... which was also the winner of a 2016 Goodreads Choice Award for Best Horror Novel.<br /><br />He writes short stories too. Some of them were gathered together in his prize-winning collection, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/373915._20th_Century_Ghosts" title=" 20th Century Ghosts" rel="nofollow noopener"> 20th Century Ghosts</a>.<br /><br />He won the Eisner Award for Best Writer for his long running comic book series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26225895._Locke___Key" title=" Locke &amp; Key" rel="nofollow noopener"> Locke &amp; Key</a>, co-created with illustrator and art wizard Gabriel Rodriguez.<br /><br />He lives in New Hampshire with a corgi named McMurtry after a certain beloved writer of cowboy tales. His next book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30251972._Strange_Weather" title=" Strange Weather" rel="nofollow noopener"> Strange Weather</a>, a collection of novellas, storms into bookstores in October of 2017.<br /></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/40296144-the-fireman">Quotes from The Fireman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;There's something horribly unfair about dying in the middle of a good story, before you have a chance to see how it all comes out. Of course, I suppose everyone ALWAYS dies in the middle of a good story, in a sense. Your own story. Or the story of your grandchildren. Death is a raw deal for narrative junkies.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7521127-there-s-something-horribly-unfair-about-dying-in-the-middle-of">84 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Your personality is not just a matter of what you know about yourself, but what others know about you. You are one person with your mother, and another with your lover, and yet another with your child. Those other people <i>create</i> you--finish you--as much as <i>you</i> create you. When you're gone, the ones you've left behind get to keep the same part of you they always had.&rdquo;</span>
